  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Elucidation</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">The height of the continuous stiffness nanoindentation measurement frequency, which corresponds to the maximum displacement or distance moved by a point on a vibrating body or wave measured from its equilibrium position. This is usually used as the region where the nanomechanical properties are extracted in continuous stiffness measurement mode.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Comment</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">The height of the continuous stiffness nanoindentation measurement frequency, which corresponds to the maximum displacement or distance moved by a point on a vibrating body or wave measured from its equilibrium position. This is usually used as the region where the nanomechanical properties are extracted in continuous stiffness measurement mode.</td>
  </tr>

    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Iri</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href="https://w3id.org/emmo/domain/nanoindentation#EMMO_2698edca-874c-5026-b61b-e7112014fdd1">https://w3id.org/emmo/domain/nanoindentation#EMMO_2698edca-874c-5026-b61b-e7112014fdd1</a></td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-annotations" colspan="2">Annotations</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Preflabel</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">Berkovich</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Elucidation</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">The Berkovich indenter tip is the most frequently used indenter tip for instrumented indentation testing (IIT) to measure mechanical properties on the nanoscale. The Berkovich indenter tip is a three-sided pyramid that can be ground to a point and thus maintains a self-similar geometry to very small scales.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Comment</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">The Berkovich indenter tip is the most frequently used indenter tip for instrumented indentation testing (IIT) to measure mechanical properties on the nanoscale. The Berkovich indenter tip is a three-sided pyramid that can be ground to a point and thus maintains a self-similar geometry to very small scales.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Label</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">Berkovich</td>
  </tr>

    <th class="element-table-formal-description" colspan="2">Formal description</th>

    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Comment</span></td>

   <div id="EMMO_3fb11ea0-8fb8-4c70-b8ec-d4e6058ae318"></div>
   <div id="ComplianceCalibrationData"></div>

ComplianceCalibrationData
^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^

.. raw:: html

  <table class="element-table">
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Iri</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href="https://w3id.org/emmo/domain/nanoindentation#EMMO_3fb11ea0-8fb8-4c70-b8ec-d4e6058ae318">https://w3id.org/emmo/domain/nanoindentation#EMMO_3fb11ea0-8fb8-4c70-b8ec-d4e6058ae318</a></td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-annotations" colspan="2">Annotations</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Preflabel</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">ComplianceCalibrationData</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Altlabel</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">SpringStiffnessCalibrationData</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Elucidation</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">The data collected by performing nanoindentation calibration tests at large applied force or depth (compliance calibration protocol), used in comparison with data provided from the equipment manufacturer in order to account of the displacement that is due to the deformation of the indentation head springs instead of the displacement into the tested sample.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Comment</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">The data collected by performing nanoindentation calibration tests at large applied force or depth (compliance calibration protocol), used in comparison with data provided from the equipment manufacturer in order to account of the displacement that is due to the deformation of the indentation head springs instead of the displacement into the tested sample.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Example</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">Intepretation of ComplianceCalibrationData into the indenter software environment to save the expected deformation of the indenter head springs during testing to correct any overestimation of the nanoindentation depth after exhaustive use of the indenter (normally compliance calibration is performed once every 1 or 2 years).</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Label</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">ComplianceCalibrationData</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-formal-description" colspan="2">Formal description</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Subclass Of</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href="https://w3id.org/emmo/domain/characterisation-methodology/chameo#CalibrationData">CalibrationData</a></td>
  </tr>
  </table>

ComplianceOffset
^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^

.. raw:: html

  <table class="element-table">
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Iri</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href="https://w3id.org/emmo/domain/nanoindentation#EMMO_d5d12433-18da-4bbb-b4ad-9b1c43b74621">https://w3id.org/emmo/domain/nanoindentation#EMMO_d5d12433-18da-4bbb-b4ad-9b1c43b74621</a></td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-annotations" colspan="2">Annotations</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Preflabel</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">ComplianceOffset</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Elucidation</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">It corresponds to the vertical drift in the z axis of the indenter head during its penetration into a sample, introduced due to the deformation of the indenter head springs, which is pronounced especially when testing hard materials.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Comment</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">It corresponds to the vertical drift in the z axis of the indenter head during its penetration into a sample, introduced due to the deformation of the indenter head springs, which is pronounced especially when testing hard materials.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Example</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">The displacement offset is the output of the compliance calibration, which calculates the deformation/displacement of indenter head springs during testing.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Label</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">ComplianceOffset</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-formal-description" colspan="2">Formal description</th>

ContactMechanicsModel
^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^

.. raw:: html

  <table class="element-table">
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Iri</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href="https://w3id.org/emmo/domain/nanoindentation#EMMO_fd9e155e-c995-5237-b930-02ad04c0208f">https://w3id.org/emmo/domain/nanoindentation#EMMO_fd9e155e-c995-5237-b930-02ad04c0208f</a></td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-annotations" colspan="2">Annotations</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Preflabel</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">ContactMechanicsModel</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Elucidation</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">It corresponds to contact mechanics model that describe the physics/mechanics of interaction between tip and sample and used to process nanoindentation raw data to extract the nanomechanical properties (i.e. stiffness, hardness, elastic modulus, etc.).</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Comment</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">It corresponds to contact mechanics model that describe the physics/mechanics of interaction between tip and sample and used to process nanoindentation raw data to extract the nanomechanical properties (i.e. stiffness, hardness, elastic modulus, etc.).</td>
  </tr>

    <td class="element-table-value">The nanoindentation data from a nanoindentation calibration test on reference sample with known indentation modulus and hardness, specifically contact depth and contact area, used to establish a function that describes the real geometry of the tip, and more specifically the tip&#x27;s area, is called Tip Area Function.</td>

  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Example</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">DisplacementCalibrationData are used to establish a polynomial regression function; the Tip Area Function. In order for the nanomechanical properties to be calculated correctly when testing a new sample, a calibration is conducted in order to obtain the Tip-Area-Function prior to every set of measurements.</td>

  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Elucidation</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">The hardness is the resistance of the sample deformation when compression forces are applied.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Comment</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">The indentation hardness is calculated by examining a material&#x27;s surface, which is being indented until an imprint is formed.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Comment</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">The hardness is the resistance of the sample deformation when compression forces are applied.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Comment</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">The indentation hardness is calculated by examining a material&#x27;s surface, which is being indented until an imprint is formed.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Example</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">The hardness of martensite can be measured using nanoindentation with a sharp indenter. The indentation depth and size are critical factors that affect the accuracy of the measurement. Martensite has a hardness range of 5-10 GPa, with some samples exhibiting higher values. The exact hardness value depends on the composition, structure, and processing history of the martensite. The values are calculated using Oliver-Pharr contact mechanics model, as a result of dividing applied force with the contact area.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Label</span></td>

    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Iri</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href="https://w3id.org/emmo/domain/nanoindentation#EMMO_d88f9767-a8a0-4f35-a584-3d0e1b153274">https://w3id.org/emmo/domain/nanoindentation#EMMO_d88f9767-a8a0-4f35-a584-3d0e1b153274</a></td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-annotations" colspan="2">Annotations</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Preflabel</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">HardnessToModulusRatio</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Elucidation</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">The outcome of dividing indentation hardness with modulus, which is related to the ratio between irreversible and reversible deformation during indentation, the materials yield strength, and the resistance to irreversible deformation, a material property which represents the energy required to create a unit volume of purely irreversible deformation.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Comment</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">The outcome of dividing indentation hardness with modulus, which is related to the ratio between irreversible and reversible deformation during indentation, the materials yield strength, and the resistance to irreversible deformation, a material property which represents the energy required to create a unit volume of purely irreversible deformation.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Example</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">Indentation hardness generally increases upon material dehydration, however to a larger extent than expected from accompanying changes in indentation modulus, thus a higher hardness to modulus ratio indicating that water acts as a plasticiser in case of examining biological materials.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Label</span></td>

   <div id="HertzModel"></div>

HertzModel
^^^^^^^^^^

.. raw:: html

  <table class="element-table">
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Iri</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href="https://w3id.org/emmo/domain/nanoindentation#EMMO_1a97a2c9-10ad-5e15-be10-fa5eabb6d542">https://w3id.org/emmo/domain/nanoindentation#EMMO_1a97a2c9-10ad-5e15-be10-fa5eabb6d542</a></td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-annotations" colspan="2">Annotations</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Preflabel</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">HertzModel</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Elucidation</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">It corresponds to Hertz contact mechanics model used to process nanoindentation raw data to extract the nanomechanical properties (i.e. stiffness, hardness, elastic modulus, etc.).</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Comment</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">The Hertz contact model produces both normal and shear forces based on the theoretical analysis of the deformation of smooth, elastic spheres in frictional contact. Viscous dashpots may be added for further energy dissipation in simulations involving impact. Both components transmit only a force.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Comment</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">It corresponds to Hertz contact mechanics model used to process nanoindentation raw data to extract the nanomechanical properties (i.e. stiffness, hardness, elastic modulus, etc.).</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Comment</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">The Hertz contact model produces both normal and shear forces based on the theoretical analysis of the deformation of smooth, elastic spheres in frictional contact. Viscous dashpots may be added for further energy dissipation in simulations involving impact. Both components transmit only a force.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Label</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">HertzModel</td>

    <td class="element-table-value">A new technique to determine the true projected contact area by nanoindentation, which requires combining two models used normally to determine the representative stress and strain from nanoindentation parameters. Consequently, it does not require any model classically used to calculate the projected contact area. The method requires performing indentation on the same sample with two indenter tips with different geometries.</td>
  </tr>

    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Elucidation</span></td>

  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Comment</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">Model fitted data correspond to the secondary data created using a contact mechanics model to extract information from the nanoindenter produced raw data.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Example</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">Typically, application of Oliver-Pharr contact mechanics model to extract from load and displacement raw data the sample stiffness, hardness, and elastic modulus.</td>

NanoindentationContactDepth
^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^

.. raw:: html

  <table class="element-table">
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Iri</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href="https://w3id.org/emmo/domain/nanoindentation#EMMO_a69e8716-a4a6-4473-a59f-146ebd991fa6">https://w3id.org/emmo/domain/nanoindentation#EMMO_a69e8716-a4a6-4473-a59f-146ebd991fa6</a></td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-annotations" colspan="2">Annotations</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Preflabel</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">NanoindentationContactDepth</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Elucidation</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">Nanoindentation contact depth describes the actual depth of contact during nanoindentation.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Comment</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">The depth measured during the indentation (h) includes the depression of the sample around the indentation, in addition to the contact depth.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Comment</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">Nanoindentation contact depth describes the actual depth of contact during nanoindentation.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Comment</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">The depth measured during the indentation (h) includes the depression of the sample around the indentation, in addition to the contact depth.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Example</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">The contact depth is calculated by subtracting from the recorded depth the elastic depth, which corresponds to the product of epsilon parameter (related to tip geometry - for Berkovich is 0.75) with applied load and devided by stiffness.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Label</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">NanoindentationContactDepth</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-formal-description" colspan="2">Formal description</th>

The regression can give the possibility for example in metals for a phase to be martensite, which can be 20%, and compared to the other potential phase, when the algorithm is fixed to assign values &lt; 50% to 0, then from regression the algorithm performs classification (the output is that the phase is not classifies as martensite).</td>

.. raw:: html

    <td class="element-table-value"><a href="https://w3id.org/emmo/domain/nanoindentation#EMMO_b4937b84-bf09-5399-8781-6b6f55fa3011">https://w3id.org/emmo/domain/nanoindentation#EMMO_b4937b84-bf09-5399-8781-6b6f55fa3011</a></td>

    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Elucidation</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">Thermal drift correction is employed in nanoindentation continuous raw data of time, displacement and load, corresponding to a stable loading sequence either in the beginning or in the end of the measurement used to measure thermal drift. The displacement change per second is measured during a constant load sequence, which corresponds to the measurement of the total displacement in the specified range of nanoindentation data, devided by the total time of the specific sequence of the routine.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Comment</span></td>

The displacement change per second is measured during a constant load sequence, which corresponds to the measurement of the total displacement in the specified range of nanoindentation data, devided by the total time of the specific sequence of the routine.</td>
  </tr>

   <div id="ThermalDriftOffset"></div>

ThermalDriftOffset
^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^

.. raw:: html

  <table class="element-table">
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Iri</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href="https://w3id.org/emmo/domain/nanoindentation#EMMO_cad806c5-2465-4bfb-8c9b-d4c0cd143f6a">https://w3id.org/emmo/domain/nanoindentation#EMMO_cad806c5-2465-4bfb-8c9b-d4c0cd143f6a</a></td>

  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-annotations" colspan="2">Annotations</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Preflabel</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">ThermalDriftOffset</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Elucidation</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">It corresponds to the vertical drift in the z axis of the indenter head during its penetration into a sample, introduced due to the thermal gradients of the tip and the sample, which is pronounced especially when testing for prolonged period of time.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Comment</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">It corresponds to the vertical drift in the z axis of the indenter head during its penetration into a sample, introduced due to the thermal gradients of the tip and the sample, which is pronounced especially when testing for prolonged period of time.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Example</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">Correction of the displacement measured during recording nanoindentation data by calculating thermal drift in nm/sec at constant force (typically 10% of the maximum applied force) for a certain time period, and substracting the mean value from the displacement data.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Label</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">ThermalDriftOffset</td>

.. raw:: html

    <td class="element-table-value">It is the z-axis calibration using a standard material with known mechanical properties to extract the contact depth versus the contact area relation to estimate the contact area without measuring it in unknown samples of their mechanical properties, according to Oliver-Pharr and ISO-14577/2022.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Comment</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">The function that describes the real geometry of the tip, and more specifically the tip&#x27;s area, is called Tip Area Function. In order for the nanomechanical properties to be calculated correctly, a calibration in order to obtain the Tip-Area-Function must be contacted prior to every set of measurements.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Comment</span></td>

In order for the nanomechanical properties to be calculated correctly, a calibration in order to obtain the Tip-Area-Function must be contacted prior to every set of measurements.</td>
  </tr>

TipMoveBack
^^^^^^^^^^^

.. raw:: html

  <table class="element-table">
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Iri</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href="https://w3id.org/emmo/domain/nanoindentation#EMMO_1e60509e-ad49-581b-8b8c-d20be3cac4b0">https://w3id.org/emmo/domain/nanoindentation#EMMO_1e60509e-ad49-581b-8b8c-d20be3cac4b0</a></td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-annotations" colspan="2">Annotations</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Preflabel</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">TipMoveBack</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Elucidation</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">The distance the indenter tip moves away from the sample surface before the indentation starts and after every single indent within a single nanoindentation measurement.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Comment</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">Typically and empirically the move back value minimum possible threshold that a user could use is ten times smaller than the interindent spacing, however most of times the value is set to a higher number because the samples are not always perfectly flat or might be tilted, which can set up a risk of the indenter tip crushing on the sample surface while moving into the nanoindenter chamber between the current and the next nanoindent location (which has distance the interindent distance) within a single nanoindentation measurement.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Comment</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">The distance the indenter tip moves away from the sample surface before the indentation starts and after every single indent within a single nanoindentation measurement.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Comment</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">Typically and empirically the move back value minimum possible threshold that a user could use is ten times smaller than the interindent spacing, however most of times the value is set to a higher number because the samples are not always perfectly flat or might be tilted, which can set up a risk of the indenter tip crushing on the sample surface while moving into the nanoindenter chamber between the current and the next nanoindent location (which has distance the interindent distance) within a single nanoindentation measurement.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Label</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">TipMoveBack</td>
  </tr>

    <th class="element-table-formal-description" colspan="2">Formal description</th>

TriggerForce

.. raw:: html

  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Iri</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value"><a href="https://w3id.org/emmo/domain/nanoindentation#EMMO_679dff53-b148-4ffa-a60c-5c9e10edee12">https://w3id.org/emmo/domain/nanoindentation#EMMO_679dff53-b148-4ffa-a60c-5c9e10edee12</a></td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <th class="element-table-annotations" colspan="2">Annotations</th>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Preflabel</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">TriggerForce</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Elucidation</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">It corresponds to the force value, which will signal to the indentation software that the indenter tip is in contact with the sample, when the force recorded by the sensor exceeds the specific threshold value.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Comment</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">It corresponds to the force value, which will signal to the indentation software that the indenter tip is in contact with the sample, when the force recorded by the sensor exceeds the specific threshold value.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Example</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">When the trigger force it is exceeded and a displacement controlled protocols is selected with specific target depth, then after that trigger force the indenter will start to count the displacement for reaching the target depth threshold and stop the measurement. In case the trigger force is relatively high, then the indentation tip will already have penetrated the sample surface in a couple of nanometers, thus technically the final nanoindentation depth will exceed the threshold of target depth control parameter.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Label</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">TriggerForce</td>
  </tr>

    <th class="element-table-formal-description" colspan="2">Formal description</th>

  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Elucidation</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">Zero contact point extrapolation is the linear regression fitted in continuous stiffness measurement in nanoindentation to identify the zero depth of the initiation of tip-sample contact in nanoindentation experiment at a specified critical contact force value ranges, used to calculate the intercept with the x-axis as the real zero contact point of the measurement.</td>
  </tr>
  <tr>
    <td class="element-table-key"><span class="element-table-key">Comment</span></td>
    <td class="element-table-value">Zero contact point extrapolation is the linear regression fitted in continuous stiffness measurement in nanoindentation to identify the zero depth of the initiation of tip-sample contact in nanoindentation experiment at a specified critical contact force value ranges, used to calculate the intercept with the x-axis as the real zero contact point of the measurement.</td>
  </tr>
